- source_description: Specifies whether to enable the payload header in the Bluetooth packet to be generated. This is applicable only for LE packets. For generating custom Bluetooth packets, set the value of this property to False. In this case, the header bits can be given as input to the Payload User Defined Bits prope

### Packet Settings:Payload Header:Header Enabled

Specifies whether to enable the payload header in the Bluetooth packet to be generated. This is applicable only for LE packets.

For generating custom Bluetooth packets, set the value of this property to **False**. In this case, the header bits can be given as input to the [Payload User Defined Bits](attr14.html) property along with the payload bits.

The default value is **True**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Header Enabled |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

| False | 0 | Specifies that the header is disabled in the generated Bluetooth packet. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| True | 1 | Specifies that the header is enabled in the generated Bluetooth packet. |

- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr47.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the settling time of the burst. The settling time is the time interval from the time when output power is 40 dB less than the final output power (X dBm) to the time when the output power is +/- 1 dB of the final output power. This value is expressed in seconds. The active packet duration f

### Power Ramp Settings:Settling Time (s)

Specifies the settling time of the burst. The settling time is the time interval from the time when output power is 40 dB less than the final output power (X dBm) to the time when the output power is +/- 1 dB of the final output power. This value is expressed in seconds. The active packet duration for LE-TP packet is 376 microseconds.

The default value is 4 microseconds. Valid values are from 1 microseconds to 20 microseconds, inclusive.

Note

The following figure shows the power ramp characteristics.

[IMAGE alt='image' src='Power-Ramp-characteristics.gif']

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Power Ramp Settling Time (s) |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | No |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`

- source_description: Specifies the ramp time of the burst. The ramp time is the time interval from the time when output power is 40 dB less than the final output power (X dBm) to the time when the output power is +/- 3 dB of the final output power. This value is expressed in seconds. The active packet duration for LE-TP

### Power Ramp Settings:Ramp Time (s)

Specifies the ramp time of the burst. The ramp time is the time interval from the time when output power is 40 dB less than the final output power (X dBm) to the time when the output power is +/- 3 dB of the final output power. This value is expressed in seconds. The active packet duration for LE-TP packet is 376 microseconds.

The default value is 2 microseconds. Valid values are from 1 microseconds to 10 microseconds, inclusive.

The following figure shows the power ramp characteristics.

[IMAGE alt='image' src='Power-Ramp-characteristics.gif']

| High-level VIs | niBT SG Set Power Ramp Settling Time, niBT SG Set Power Ramp Time |
| Resettable | No |

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr5.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr5.html

- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Returns the sample rate, in samples per second (S/s), for generation. The symbol rate of the Bluetooth signal is 1 megasymbol per second. The sample rate of the generated signal is the product of the symbol rate and the oversampling factor. The BT Generation uses an oversampling factor of 8. Remarks

### Hardware Settings:Recommended Settings:IQ Rate (S/s)

Returns the sample rate, in samples per second (S/s), for generation. The symbol rate of the Bluetooth signal is 1 megasymbol per second. The sample rate of the generated signal is the product of the symbol rate and the oversampling factor. The BT Generation uses an oversampling factor of 8.

#### Remarks

| Resettable | No |

### Packet Settings:Direction Finding:Antenna Switching Pattern

Specifies the pattern in which the antennas switch in constant tone extension (CTE) portion of the low energy (LE) packet. The current definition always treats A0 as the reference antenna. A1, A2, A3...Am are all non-reference antennas. This property is applicable only when you set the [Antenna Switching Enabled](/csh?topicname=attr56.html) to **True**.

The default value is A0.

Remarks The following table lists the characteristics of this property. Short Name CS Packet Format Data type ci32.png Permissio

### Packet Settings:Channel Sounding:Packet Format

Specifies the channel sounding (CS) packet format. This property is applicable only when you set the packet type to either **LE-CS-1M** or **LE-CS-2M**.

The default value is **SYNC**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | CS Packet Format |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

| SYNC | 0 | Specifies that the CS packet format is SYNC. This packet consists of preamble, CS access address, trailer and sounding sequence field. The sounding sequence field is optional. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| CS Tone | 1 | Specifies that the CS packet format is CS Tone. This packet consists of unmodulated carrier. |
| CS Tone after SYNC | 2 | Specifies that the CS packet format is CS Tone after SYNC. This packet consists of SYNC followed by a CS Tone. |
| CS Tone before SYNC | 3 | Specifies that the CS packet format is CS Tone before SYNC. This packet consists of CS Tone followed by a SYNC. |

## TOPIC 00090: Packet Settings:Channel Sounding:Sequence Marker Signals []

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr60.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr60.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies an array of sounding sequence marker signals. This property is applicable only when you set the CS SYNC Sequence to Sounding Sequence. When sounding sequence length property is set to 32, only the first element shall be inserted in the sounding sequence, and remaining elements shall be dis

### Packet Settings:Channel Sounding:Sequence Marker Signals []

Specifies an array of sounding sequence marker signals. This property is applicable only when you set the CS SYNC Sequence to **Sounding Sequence.**

When sounding sequence length property is set to 32, only the first element shall be inserted in the sounding sequence, and remaining elements shall be discarded.

When sounding sequence length property is set to 96, up to the first two elements shall be inserted in the sounding sequence, and remaining elements shall be discarded.

The default value is **1100**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Sounding Sequence Marker Signals [] |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

| 1100 | 0 | Specifies that the sounding sequence marker signal inserted in the sounding sequence is 1100. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 0011 | 1 | Specifies that the sounding sequence marker signal inserted in the sounding sequence is 0011. |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr61.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00091: Packet Settings:Channel Sounding:Sequence Marker Positions []

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr61.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr61.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies an array of sounding sequence marker positions at which sounding sequence marker signals are inserted. This property is applicable only when you set the CS SYNC Sequence to Sounding Sequence. When sounding sequence length property is set to 32, only the first element from the sounding sequ

### Packet Settings:Channel Sounding:Sequence Marker Positions []

Specifies an array of sounding sequence marker positions at which sounding sequence marker signals are inserted. This property is applicable only when you set the CS SYNC Sequence to **Sounding Sequence.**

When sounding sequence length property is set to 32, only the first element from the sounding sequence marker positions array is considered, and remaining elements are discarded. Valid values are from 0 to 28.

When sounding sequence length property is set to 96, up to the first two elements from sounding sequence marker positions array are considered and remaining elements are discarded. Valid values for array index 0 are from 0 to 63 and for array index 1 are from 67 to 92.

The default value is **0**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Sounding Sequence Marker Positions [] |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

### Packet Settings:High Data Throughput:Physical Channel Address

Specifies the 40-bit physical channel address of Higher Data Throughput (HDT) packet.

The default value is 0x9F15555555.

## TOPIC 00104: Packet Settings:Payload Header:Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr6e.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr6e.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the payload zone configuration mode for the LE-HDT packet when HDT Packet Format is set to Format1. The default value is Auto. Remarks The following table lists the characteristics of this property. Short Name Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode Data type ci32.png Permissions Read/Writ

### Packet Settings:Payload Header:Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode

Specifies the payload zone configuration mode for the LE-HDT packet when [HDT Packet Format](/csh?topicname=attr67.html) is set to **Format1**.

The default value is Auto.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

| Auto | 0 | Specifies that the payload zone length is computed based on the Payload Length Mode and Payload Length. When Payload Length Mode property is set to Maximum Length, the maximum payload length is used for the specified Number of Payloads. When Payload Length Mode property is set to User Defined, the user configured Payload Length(s) is used for specified Number of Payloads. In this mode, the block size, number of blocks, last block size and TxBlockMap fields are computed instead of being entered by the user. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| User Defined | 1 | Specifies that the payload zone length is configured using the channel specific properties such as Number of Blocks, Block Size, Last Block Size, TxBlock Map. |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

## TOPIC 00105: Packet Settings:Payload Header:TxLen Sequence Number

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr6f.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr6f.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the value of TxLen SN field of Tx Portion of PDU Header. This property is valid only for the LE-HDT packet when HDT Packet Format is set to Format1 and Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode is set to User Defined. You must use "payload x" as the active channel string to configure this pr

### Packet Settings:Payload Header:TxLen Sequence Number

Specifies the value of TxLen SN field of Tx Portion of PDU Header. This property is valid only for the LE-HDT packet when [HDT Packet Format](/csh?topicname=attr67.html) is set to **Format1** and [Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode](/csh?topicname=attr6e.html) is set to **User Defined**.

You must use "payload x" as the active channel string to configure this property.

The default value is **11**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | TxLen Sequence Number |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

| 00 | 0 | Specifies that the packet does not include a payload or any of its blocks. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 01 | 1 | Specifies that the payload has 1 block and the Payload Length is Last Block Size. |
| 10 | 2 | Specifies that the payload can have maximum 8 blocks and only bits 0 to 7 of TxBlock Map are explicit; bits 8 to 15 are always zero. |
| 11 | 3 | Specifies that the payload can have maximum 16 blocks. |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

## TOPIC 00106: Packet Settings:Packet Type

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr7.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr7.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the Bluetooth packet type. The default value is DH1. Remarks The following table lists the characteristics of this property. Short Name Packet Type Data type ci32.png Permissions Read/Write High-level VIs niBT SG Set Packet Type Resettable Yes NULL 0 Specifies that the packet type is NULL.

### Packet Settings:Packet Type

Specifies the Bluetooth packet type.

The default value is **DH1**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Packet Type |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | niBT SG Set Packet Type |
| Resettable | Yes |

| NULL | 0 | Specifies that the packet type is NULL. This packet has no payload and consists of the channel access code and packet header only. Refer to Section 6.5.1.2, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| POLL | 1 | Specifies that the packet type is POLL. The POLL packet does not have a payload. Refer to Section 6.5.1.3, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| FHS | 2 | Specifies that the packet type is frequency hop synchronization (FHS). The FHS packet is a special control packet containing the Bluetooth device address and the sender's clock. Refer to Section 6.5.1.4, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DM1 | 3 | Specifies that the packet type is DM1. The DM1 packet carries only data information. The information and cyclic redundancy check (CRC) bits are coded with a rate 2/3 FEC. The DM1 packet occupies a single time slot. Refer to Sections 6.5.1.5 and 6.5.4.1, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DH1 | 4 | Specifies that the packet type is DH1. This packet is similar to the DM1 packet, except that the information in the payload is not forward error correction (FEC) encoded. The DH1 packet occupies a single time slot. Refer to Sections 6.5.1.5 and 6.5.4.2, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 2-DH1 | 5 | Specifies that the packet type is 2-DH1. This packet is similar to the DH1 packet, except that the information in the payload is modulated using pi/4-QPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.4.8, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| HV1 | 6 | Specifies that the packet type is HV1. The HV1 packet has 10 information bytes. Refer to Section 6.5.2.1, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| HV2 | 7 | Specifies that the packet type is HV2. The HV2 packet has 20 information bytes. Refer to Section 6.5.2.3, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 2-EV3 | 8 | Specifies that the packet type is 2-EV3. This packet is similar to the EV3 packet, except that the payload is modulated using pi/4-DQPSK. It has 1 and 60 information bytes, inclusive, and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.3.4, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| HV3 | 9 | Specifies that the packet type is HV3. The HV3 packet has 30 information bytes. The information bytes are not protected by forward error correction (FEC). Refer to Section 6.5.2.3, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| EV3 | 10 | Specifies that the packet type is EV3. The EV3 packet has 1 to 30 information bytes, inclusive, and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.3.1, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 3-EV3 | 11 | Specifies that the packet type is 3-EV3. The 3-EV3 packet is similar to the EV3 packet, except that the payload is modulated using 8-DPSK. The 3-EV3 packet has 1 to 90 information bytes, inclusive and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.3.6, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DV | 12 | Specifies that the packet type is data voice (DV). The DV packet is a combined data-voice packet. Refer to Section 6.5.2.4, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 3-DH1 | 13 | Specifies that the packet type is 3-DH1. This packet is similar to the DH1 packet, except that the payload is modulated using 8-DPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.4.11, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| AUX1 | 14 | Specifies that the packet type is AUX1. This packet resembles a DH1 packet but has no CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.4.7, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DM3 | 15 | Specifies that the packet type is DM3. This packet may occupy up to three time slots. The payload has 2 to 123 information bytes, inclusive (including the 2-byte payload header) and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.4.3, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 2-DH3 | 16 | Specifies that the packet type is 2-DH3. This packet is similar to the DH3 packet, except that the payload is modulated using pi/4-DQPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.4.9, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DH3 | 17 | Specifies that the packet type is DH3. This packet is similar to the DM3 packet, except that the information in the payload is not forward error correction (FEC) encoded. Refer to Section 6.5.4.4, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 3-DH3 | 18 | Specifies that the packet type is 3-DH3. This packet is similar to the DH3 packet, except that the payload is modulated using 8-DPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.4.12, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| EV4 | 19 | Specifies that the packet type is EV4. The EV4 packet has 1 to 120 information bytes, inclusive, and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.3.2, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 2-EV5 | 20 | Specifies that the packet type is 2-EV5. The 2-EV5 packet is similar to the EV5 packet, except that the payload is modulated using pi/4-DQPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.3.5, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| EV5 | 21 | Specifies that the packet type is EV5. The EV5 packet has 1 to 180 information bytes, inclusive, and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.3.3, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 3-EV5 | 22 | Specifies that the packet type is 3-EV5. The 3-EV5 packet is similar to the EV5 packet, except that the payload is modulated using 8-DPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.3.7, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DM5 | 23 | Specifies that the packet type is DM5. The payload has 2 to 226 information bytes (including the 2-byte payload header), inclusive, and a 16-bit CRC code. Refer to Section 6.5.4.6, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 2-DH5 | 24 | Specifies that the packet type is 2-DH5. This packet is similar to the DH5 packet, except that the payload is modulated using pi/4-DQPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.4.10, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| DH5 | 25 | Specifies that the packet type is DH5. This packet is similar to the DM5 packet, except that the information in the payload is not forward error correction (FEC) encoded. Refer to Section 6.5.4.6, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| 3-DH5 | 26 | Specifies that the packet type is 3-DH5. This packet is similar to the DH5 packet, except that the payload is modulated using 8DPSK. Refer to Section 6.5.4.13, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-TP | 27 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-TP. Refer to Section 2.1, Part B, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v4.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-TP-EXT | 28 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-TP-EXT. This packet is similar to the LE-TP packet, except that the payload length is extended up to 8191 bytes. For payload length up to 255 bytes, typical LE packet is generated. For payload length greater than 255 bytes, Hyper Length LE packet is generated. Refer to Section 2.1, Part B, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-Enhanced | 29 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-Enhanced. This is an LE packet type with a symbol rate of 2 Ms/s and maximum payload length of 8191 bytes. For payload length up to 255 bytes, typical LE packet is generated. For payload length greater than 255 bytes, Hyper Length LE packet is generated. Refer to Section 2.1, Part B, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-LR-125k | 30 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-LR-125k. This is an LE packet type which supports long range communication at a data rate of 125 kbps. Refer to Section 2.2, Part B, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-LR-500k | 31 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-LR-500k. This is an LE packet type which supports long range communication at a data rate of 500 kbps. Refer to Section 2.2, Part B, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-CS-1M | 32 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-CS-1M. This is a LE packet type which supports channel sounding feature at a data rate of 1Ms/s.Refer to Section 2, Part H, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-CS-2M | 33 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-CS-2M. This is a LE packet type which supports channel sounding feature at a data rate of 2Ms/s.Refer to Section 2, Part H, Volume 6 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| LE-HDT | 34 | Specifies that the packet type is LE-HDT. This is a LE packet type which supports higher data rates (2 Mbps, 3 Mbps, 4 Mbps, 6 Mbps, and 7.5 Mbps). |
| ID | 254 | Specifies that the packet type is ID. The identity, or ID, packet consists of the device access code (DAC) or inquiry access code (IAC). Refer to Section 6.5.1.1, Part B, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification v6.0 for more information about this packet. |
| Idle | 255 | Specifies that the packet type is Idle. This packet type is not defined in the Bluetooth Specification v6.0. You can use this packet to create empty slots between Bluetooth packets. |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

## TOPIC 00110: Packet Settings:Payload Header:TxBlock Map

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr73.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr73.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the TxBlockMap field of Tx Portion of PDU Header. The TxBlockMap field is 8 or 16 bits depending on the value of TxLen Sequence Number. It indicates which blocks are actually being transmitted in the packet, with bit b set to 1 if block b (counting from 0) is included and 0 if it is not. A

### Packet Settings:Payload Header:TxBlock Map

Specifies the TxBlockMap field of Tx Portion of PDU Header. The TxBlockMap field is 8 or 16 bits depending on the value of [TxLen Sequence Number](/csh?topicname=attr6f.html). It indicates which blocks are actually being transmitted in the packet, with bit b set to 1 if block b (counting from 0) is included and 0 if it is not. At least one bit shall be set.

This property is valid only for the LE-HDT packet when [HDT Packet Format](attr67.html) is set to **Format1** and [Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode](attr6e.html) is set to **User Defined**.

You must use "payload x" as the active channel string to configure this property.

The default value is **0xFFFF**.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | TxBlock Map |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | Yes |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

## TOPIC 00111: Active Channel

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attr74.html`

- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`

- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the active channel string used to access all subsequent properties in a property node until a new active channel is specified. If the property you want to use is channel-specific, you must first select the Active Channel property and then pass the name of the specific channel. If you speci

### Active Channel

Specifies the [active channel](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_btgen_config_gen_active_channel_lv) string used to access all subsequent properties in a property node until a new active channel is specified.

If the property you want to use is channel-specific, you must first select the Active Channel property and then pass the name of the specific channel. If you specify an active channel for a property that is not channel-specific, the BT Generation returns an error.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Active Channel |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Write Only |
| High-level VIs | N/A |
| Resettable | No |

Parent topic:

## TOPIC 00117: Packet Settings:Packet Header:LT Address

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attrb.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attrb.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Specifies the 3-bit logical transport (LT) address of the packet. The LT address field indicates the destination slave for a packet in a master-to-slave transmission slot and indicates the source slave for a slave-to-master transmission slot. Refer to sections 6.4.1 and 6.4.2, Part B, Volume 2 of th

### Packet Settings:Packet Header:LT Address

Specifies the 3-bit logical transport (LT) address of the packet. The LT address field indicates the destination slave for a packet in a master-to-slave transmission slot and indicates the source slave for a slave-to-master transmission slot. Refer to sections 6.4.1 and 6.4.2, Part B, Volume 2 of the *Bluetooth Specification v6.0* for more information about the LT address of a packet.

The default value is 0. Valid values are 0 to 7, inclusive.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Packet Header LT Address |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | niBT SG Set Packet Header LT Address |
| Resettable | Yes |

Parent topic:

niBTGeneration Properties

### Packet Settings:Packet Header:FLOW

Specifies the value for the flow control field in the packet header. This field controls the 1-bit flow control parameter in the packet. Refer to Section 6.4.3, Part B, Volume 2 of the *Bluetooth Specification v6.0* for more information about the flow control field.

The default value is 0. Valid values are 0, which indicates a Stop condition, and 1, which indicates a Go condition.

### Packet Settings:Packet Header:ARQN

| NAK | 0 | Specifies a negative acknowledgement. |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ACK | 1 | Specifies a positive acknowledgement. |

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attrf.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/resource/objmgr/nibtgeneration-rc/nibtgeneration/attrf.html

### Packet Settings:Payload Header:LLID

Specifies whether the payload is the start or continuation fragment of a logical link control and adaptation protocol (L2CAP) or link management protocol (LMP) message.

You must use "payload x" as the active channel string to configure this property for the LE-HDT packet when [HDT Packet Format](attr67.html) is set to **Format1** and [Format1 Payload Zone Configuration Mode](attr6e.html) is set to **User Defined**.

The default value is 0. Valid values are 0, 1, 2, and 3.

#### Remarks

The following table lists the [characteristics](/csh?productcategories=147794&context=lvcore_lvprop_flags) of this property.

| Short Name | Payload Header LLID |
| --- | --- |
| Data type |  |
| Permissions | Read/Write |
| High-level VIs | niBT SG Set Payload Header LLID |
| Resettable | Yes |

### niBT RFSG Create and Download Waveform VI

#### Inputs/Outputs

Use this parameter to configure the behavior and operation of the appropriate BT Generation VI that accepts the niBT SG session refnum at its input. instrument handle — instrument handle identifies the instrument session. The BT Generation obtains this parameter from the niRFSG Initialize VI or the niRFSG Initialize With Options VI. waveform name — waveform name specifies the name used to store the waveform. This string is case-insensitive and alphanumeric, and does not use reserved words. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. niBT SG session out — niBT SG session out returns the niBT SG session refnum. Use this reference as the session input to subsequent VIs. Note Close the niBT SG session refnum using the niBT SG Close Session VI before the VI completes execution to avoid possible memory leak issues. instrument handle out — instrument handle out passes a reference from the instrument session to the next VI. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-channel-number-to-carrier-frequency-vi.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00133: niBT SG Channel Number to Carrier Frequency VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-channel-number-to-carrier-frequency-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-channel-number-to-carrier-frequency-vi.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Computes the carrier frequency of the Bluetooth signal to generate based on the value that you specify in the channel number parameter. The BT Generation computes the center frequency according to section 2, Part A, Volume 2 of the Bluetooth Specification Version v6.0. The Bluetooth system operates

### niBT SG Channel Number to Carrier Frequency VI

Computes the carrier frequency of the Bluetooth signal to generate based on the value that you specify in the **channel number** parameter. The BT Generation computes the center frequency according to section 2, Part A, Volume 2 of the *Bluetooth Specification Version v6.0*.

The Bluetooth system operates in the 2.4 GHz ISM band. This frequency band is 2,400 MHz to 2,483.5 MHz. RF channels are spaced 1 MHz apart and are ordered in channel number *k* according to the following formula:

*f* = 2402+*k* MHz

where

*k*=0, 1, ..., 78 for Basic Rate/Enhanced Data Rate packets

*f* = 2402+(2**k*) MHz

where

*k*=0, 1, ..., 39 for Low Energy packet

*f* is the frequency of the RF channels.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-channel-number-to-carrier-frequency-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| channel number — channel number specifies the channel number. standard — standard specifies the standard. The default value is Basic+EDR. Basic+EDR (0) Specifies that the standard is basic rate or enhanced data rate (EDR). LE (1) Specifies that the standard is low energy (LE). error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. carrier frequency (Hz) — carrier frequency returns the RF frequency (f) corresponding to the channel number k, where f = 2402 + k MHz. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |  |
| --- | --- |
| Basic+EDR (0) | Specifies that the standard is basic rate or enhanced data rate (EDR). |
| LE (1) | Specifies that the standard is low energy (LE). |

Parent topic:

Generation

## TOPIC 00135: niBT SG Create and Write Waveforms to File VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-create-and-write-waveforms-to-file-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-create-and-write-waveforms-to-file-vi.html

- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Creates waveforms according to the parameters you specify, and saves the waveforms to a file. In addition to the waveform, this VI also saves the Headroom and IQ Rate properties to the file. icon Inputs/Outputs cgenclassrn.png niBT SG session niBT SG session specifies the niBT SG session refnum. cpa

### niBT SG Create and Write Waveforms to File VI

Creates waveforms according to the parameters you specify, and saves the waveforms to a file.

In addition to the waveform, this VI also saves the [Headroom](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_lvbtgenprop_attr4) and [IQ Rate](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_lvbtgenprop_attr5) properties to the file.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-create-and-write-waveforms-to-file-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| niBT SG session — niBT SG session specifies the niBT SG session refnum. file path — file path specifies the absolute path to the file to which the BT Generation saves the waveforms. operation — operation specifies the operation to perform on the file. The default value is create or replace. open (0) Opens an existing file to write the niBT SG session property values. open or create (1) Opens an existing file or creates a new file if the file does not exist. create or replace (2) Creates a new file or replaces an existing file. create (3) Creates a new file. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. niBT SG session out — niBT SG session out returns the niBT SG session refnum. Use this reference as the session input to subsequent VIs. Note Close the niBT SG session refnum using the niBT SG Close Session VI before the VI completes execution to avoid possible memory leak issues. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |  |
| --- | --- |
| open (0) | Opens an existing file to write the niBT SG session property values. |
| open or create (1) | Opens an existing file or creates a new file if the file does not exist. |
| create or replace (2) | Creates a new file or replaces an existing file. |
| create (3) | Creates a new file. |

Parent topic:

File IO

This output provides standard error out functionality. |

## TOPIC 00137: niBT SG Load Configuration from File VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-load-configuration-from-file-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-load-configuration-from-file-vi.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Reads values of session properties (configuration) saved in a file and sets these values to the corresponding properties on the session, thus restoring the state of the BT Generation to the original state when the file was saved. icon Inputs/Outputs cbool.png reset session? reset session specifies w

### niBT SG Load Configuration from File VI

Reads values of session properties (configuration) saved in a file and sets these values to the corresponding properties on the session, thus restoring the state of the BT Generation to the original state when the file was saved.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-load-configuration-from-file-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| reset session? — reset session specifies whether the BT Generation must reset all the properties of the session to their default values before setting the new values specified in the file. The default value is TRUE. niBT SG session — niBT SG session specifies the niBT SG session refnum. file path — file path specifies the absolute path to the file from which the BT Generation loads the configuration. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. niBT SG session out — niBT SG session out returns the niBT SG session refnum. Use this reference as the session input to subsequent VIs. Note Close the niBT SG session refnum using the niBT SG Close Session VI before the VI completes execution to avoid possible memory leak issues. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |
| --- |

Parent topic:

File IO

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-open-session-vi.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00138: niBT SG Open Session VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-open-session-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-open-session-vi.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Looks up an existing niBT SG session using the session name parameter and returns the refnum that you can pass to subsequent niBT SG VIs and the niBT SG Property Node. If the look up fails, the niBT SG Open Session VI creates a new niBT SG session and returns a new refnum. icon Inputs/Outputs cstr.p

### niBT SG Open Session VI

Looks up an existing niBT SG session using the **session name** parameter and returns the refnum that you can pass to subsequent niBT SG VIs and the [niBT SG Property Node](/csh?topicname=nibt-sg-property-node-vi.html). If the look up fails, the niBT SG Open Session VI creates a new niBT SG session and returns a new refnum.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-open-session-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| session name — session name specifies the name of the session that you are looking up or creating. If a session with the same name already exists, this VI returns a reference to that session. To get the reference to an already-opened session x, specify x as the session name. You can obtain the reference to an existing session multiple times if you have not called the niBT SG Close Session VI in that session. You do not need to close the session multiple times. To create an unnamed session, pass an empty string to the session name parameter or leave this parameter unwired. Tip National Instruments recommends that you call the niBT SG Close Session VI for each uniquely named instance of the niBT SG Open Session VI or each instance of the niBT SG Open Session VI with an unnamed session. toolkit compatibility version — toolkit compatibility version specifies the version of the BT Generation to which the current version of the BT Generation is compatible. If the behavior of the BT Generation changes in a new version, use this parameter to specify that you want to continue using the behavior of the previous release. 1.0.0 (10000) Specifies that the current version of the BT Generation is compatible with 1.0.0. 2.0.0 (20000) Specifies that the current version of the BT Generation is compatible with 2.0.0. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. niBT SG session out — niBT SG session out returns the niBT SG session refnum. Use this reference as the session input to subsequent VIs. Note Close the niBT SG session refnum using the niBT SG Close Session VI before the VI completes execution to avoid possible memory leak issues. new session? — new session? indicates whether the VI creates a new session. TRUE Indicates that the VI creates a new session. FALSE Indicates that the VI returns a reference to an existing session. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |  |
| --- | --- |
| 1.0.0 (10000) | Specifies that the current version of the BT Generation is compatible with 1.0.0. |
| 2.0.0 (20000) | Specifies that the current version of the BT Generation is compatible with 2.0.0. |
| TRUE | Indicates that the VI creates a new session. |
| FALSE | Indicates that the VI returns a reference to an existing session. |

Parent topic:

Generation

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-read-waveform-from-file-vi.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00140: niBT SG Read Waveform from File VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-read-waveform-from-file-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-read-waveform-from-file-vi.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Reads a waveform from a TDMS file. You can save this file using the Generation Interactive Example for Bluetooth. The niBT SG Read Waveform from File VI returns the I/Q complex waveform data that you can subsequently download to an RF signal generator device. In addition to the I/Q complex waveform

### niBT SG Read Waveform from File VI

Reads a waveform from a TDMS file. You can save this file using the *Generation Interactive Example for Bluetooth*. The niBT SG Read Waveform from File VI returns the I/Q complex waveform data that you can subsequently download to an RF signal generator device.

In addition to the I/Q complex waveform data, the *Generation Interactive Example for Bluetooth* also saves the [Headroom](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_lvbtgenprop_attr4) and [IQ Rate](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_lvbtgenprop_attr5) properties of the waveform to the file. Use the niBT SG Read Waveform from File VI or TDMS file properties in your programming environment to read the values of these properties. The NI_RF_Headroom and NI_RF_IQRate properties are located in the following locations within the TDMS file.

| Property Name | Datatype | Group Name | Channel Name |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| NI_RF_IQRate | float64 | waveforms | niBT SG Waveform |
| NI_RF_Headroom | float64 | waveforms | niBT SG Waveform |

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-read-waveform-from-file-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| count (-1: all) — count specifies the maximum number of samples of the I/Q complex waveform to read from the file. The default value is -1, which returns all samples. If you set count to 1,000 and offset to 2, the VI returns 1,000 samples, starting from index 2 and ending at index 1,002. offset (0) — offset specifies the number of samples into the waveform at which the VI begins reading the I/Q data. The default value is 0. If you set count to 1,000 and offset to 2, the VI returns 1,000 samples, starting from index 2 and ending at index 1,002. file path — file path specifies the complete path to the TDMS file from which the BT Generation reads the waveform. waveform name — waveform name specifies the name of the waveform to read from the file. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. complex waveform — complex waveform returns the baseband time-domain waveform. t0 — t0 returns the starting time, in seconds. dt — dt returns the time interval, in seconds, between baseband I/Q samples. y — y returns the array of baseband complex I/Q samples. IQ rate (S/s) — IQ rate returns the I/Q rate, in samples per second (S/s), of the waveform. headroom (dB) — headroom returns the headroom, in dB, of the waveform. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. eof — eof returns whether the end of file has been reached with this read. |
| --- |
| t0 — t0 returns the starting time, in seconds. dt — dt returns the time interval, in seconds, between baseband I/Q samples. y — y returns the array of baseband complex I/Q samples. |

Parent topic:

File IO

## TOPIC 00142: niBT SG Save Configuration to File VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-save-configuration-to-file-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/nibt-sg-save-configuration-to-file-vi.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Saves properties of the session, which you may have modified after opening the session, to a file located at the specified path. You can use this VI to save the current state of the BT Generation session to a file. You can later load the saved configuration using the niBT SG Load Configuration from

### niBT SG Save Configuration to File VI

Saves properties of the session, which you may have modified after opening the session, to a file located at the specified path.

You can use this VI to save the current state of the BT Generation session to a file. You can later load the saved configuration using the [niBT SG Load Configuration from File](nibt-sg-load-configuration-from-file-vi.html) VI.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-save-configuration-to-file-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| niBT SG session — niBT SG session specifies the niBT SG session refnum. file path — file path specifies the absolute path to the TDMS file to which the BT Generation saves the configuration. operation — operation specifies the operation to perform on the file. The default value is create or replace. open (0) Opens an existing file to write the niBT SG session property values. open or create (1) Opens an existing file or creates a new file if the file does not exist. create or replace (2) Creates a new file or replaces an existing file. create (3) Creates a new file. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. niBT SG session out — niBT SG session out returns the niBT SG session refnum. Use this reference as the session input to subsequent VIs. Note Close the niBT SG session refnum using the niBT SG Close Session VI before the VI completes execution to avoid possible memory leak issues. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |  |
| --- | --- |
| open (0) | Opens an existing file to write the niBT SG session property values. |
| open or create (1) | Opens an existing file or creates a new file if the file does not exist. |
| create or replace (2) | Creates a new file or replaces an existing file. |
| create (3) | Creates a new file. |

Parent topic:

File IO

- source_description: Clears the properties stored in the RFSG database and clears the waveforms from the NI RF vector signal generator memory. ### niBT RFSG Clear Database VI

Clears the properties stored in the [RFSG database](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_btgen_rfsg_database) and clears the waveforms from the NI RF vector signal generator memory.

This VI clears the waveform and properties of the waveform that you specify in the **waveform name** parameter. If you set the **waveform name** parameter to an empty string, this VI clears all the waveforms and their properties.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-rfsg-clear-database-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| instrument handle — instrument handle identifies the instrument session. The BT Generation obtains this parameter from the niRFSG Initialize VI or the niRFSG Initialize With Options VI. waveform name — waveform name specifies the name of the waveform to clear. If you set this parameter to an empty string, the VI clears all the waveforms and their properties. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. instrument handle out — instrument handle out passes a reference from the instrument session to the next VI. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |
| --- |

Parent topic:

The VI sets the niRFSG Power Level property to the sum of the power le

### niBT RFSG Configure Script VI

Configures the I/Q rate and power level of the waveforms that you specify in the **script** parameter. This VI sets the niRFSG IQ Rate property to the I/Q rate in the [RFSG database](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_btgen_rfsg_database) if the I/Q rates are the same for all the waveforms. The VI sets the niRFSG Power Level property to the sum of the power level that you specify in the **power level** parameter and the minimum headrooms of all the waveforms.

Note

niBT SG Create and Write Waveforms to File

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-rfsg-configure-script-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| instrument handle — instrument handle identifies the instrument session. The BT Generation obtains this parameter from the niRFSG Initialize VI or the niRFSG Initialize With Options VI. — script specifies the script that controls waveform generation. NI-RFSG supports multiple scripts that you can select using the niRFSG Selected Script property. power level (dBm) — power level specifies the power level, in dBm. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. instrument handle out — instrument handle out passes a reference from the instrument session to the next VI. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |
| --- |

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`

- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Stores the headroom, which you specify in the headroom parameter, in the RFSG database. icon Inputs/Outputs civrn.png instrument handle instrument handle identifies the instrument session. The BT Generation obtains this parameter from the niRFSG Initialize VI or the niRFSG Initialize With Options VI

### niBT RFSG Store Headroom VI

Stores the headroom, which you specify in the **headroom** parameter, in the [RFSG database](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_btgen_rfsg_database).

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-rfsg-store-headroom-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| instrument handle — instrument handle identifies the instrument session. The BT Generation obtains this parameter from the niRFSG Initialize VI or the niRFSG Initialize With Options VI. waveform name — waveform name specifies the name of the waveform for which you want to store the headroom. The BT Generation uses the waveform name parameter as the key to store the waveform properties in the RFSG database. headroom (dB) — headroom specifies the headroom, in dB, to store in the RFSG database. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. instrument handle out — instrument handle out passes a reference from the instrument session to the next VI. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |
| --- |

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/standard-functionality-for-error-in-parameters.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00151: Using the Standard Functionality for error in Parameters

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/standard-functionality-for-error-in-parameters.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/standard-functionality-for-error-in-parameters.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Many LabVIEW nodes such as VIs contain error in parameters you can use to manage errors. These parameters typically provide the same, standard functionality. When a node exhibits different parameter functionality, the exceptions are documented in the reference material for that node. Standard error

### Using the Standard Functionality for error in Parameters

Many LabVIEW nodes such as VIs contain error in parameters you can use to manage errors. These parameters typically provide the same, standard functionality. When a node exhibits different parameter functionality, the exceptions are documented in the reference material for that node. Standard error in behavior is as follows

Note

error in

error in

|  | error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. The default is no error. If an error occurred before this node runs, the node passes the error in value to error out. This node runs normally only if no error occurred before this node runs. If an error occurs while this node runs, it runs normally and sets its own error status in error out. Use error in and error out to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring error out from one node to error in of the next node. |
| --- | --- |

The error in cluster contains the following cluster elements:

|  | status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred before this node ran or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred before this node ran. The default is FALSE. |
| --- | --- |
|  | code is the error or warning code. The default is 0. If status is TRUE, code is an error code. If status is FALSE, code is 0 or a warning code. |
|  | source specifies the origin of the error or warning and is, in most cases, the name of the node that produced the error or warning. The default is an empty string. |

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/standard-functionality-for-error-out-parameters.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00152: Using the Standard Functionality for error out Parameters

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/standard-functionality-for-error-out-parameters.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/standard-functionality-for-error-out-parameters.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Many LabVIEW nodes such as VIs contain an error out parameter you can use to manage errors. These parameters typically provide the same, standard functionality. When a node exhibits different parameter functionality, the exceptions are documented in the reference material for that node. Standard err

### Using the Standard Functionality for error out Parameters

Many LabVIEW nodes such as VIs contain an error out parameter you can use to manage errors. These parameters typically provide the same, standard functionality. When a node exhibits different parameter functionality, the exceptions are documented in the reference material for that node.

Standard error out functionality is as follows:

|  | error out contains error information. If error in indicates that an error occurred before this VI ran, error out contains the same error information. Otherwise, it describes the error status that this VI or function produces. Right-click the error out front panel indicator and select Explain Error from the shortcut menu for more information about the error. |
| --- | --- |

error out contains the following cluster elements:

|  | status is TRUE (X) if an error occurred before this node ran or during the running of this node or FALSE (checkmark) to indicate a warning or that no error occurred before this node ran or during the running of this node. |
| --- | --- |
|  | code is the error or warning code. If status is TRUE, code is an error code. If status is FALSE, code is 0 or a warning code. |
|  | source specifies the origin of the error or warning and is, in most cases, the name of the node that produced the error or warning. |

<!--NI_TOPIC bundle=rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref path=vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/sys/nibt-sg-set-antenna-relative-phase-and-amplitude-vi.html language=enus -->
## TOPIC 00158: niBT SG Set Antenna Relative Phase and Amplitude VI

- bundle_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- source_path: `vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/sys/nibt-sg-set-antenna-relative-phase-and-amplitude-vi.html`
- source_url: https://docs-be.ni.com/bundle/rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref/raw/resource/enus/vi-lib/rf-toolkits/bt/sg/sys/nibt-sg-set-antenna-relative-phase-and-amplitude-vi.html
- document_id: `rfmxbtgen-labview-api-ref`
- page_type: `leaf`
- content_type: `reference`
- source_description: Sets the Relative Phase and Relative Amplitude values for the non reference antennas An (1<n<=256) relative to the reference antenna A0, only when you set the Antenna Switching Enabled property True. The reference period and sampling slots in the constant tone extension (CTE) field are modulated in

### niBT SG Set Antenna Relative Phase and Amplitude VI

Sets the **Relative Phase** and **Relative Amplitude** values for the non reference antennas An (1<n<=256) relative to the reference antenna A0, only when you set the [Antenna Switching Enabled](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_lvbtgenprop_attr56) property **True**. The reference period and sampling slots in the constant tone extension (CTE) field are modulated in amplitude and phase as specified in the [Antenna Switching Pattern](/csh?context=rfmxbtgen_lvbtgenprop_attr55) property.

[IMAGE alt='icon' src='nibt-sg-set-antenna-relative-phase-and-amplitude-vi.png']

#### Inputs/Outputs

| niBT SG session — niBT SG session specifies the niBT SG session refnum. Use this parameter to configure the behavior and operation of the appropriate BT Generation VI that accepts the niBT SG session refnum at its input. relative phase (deg) — relative phase specifies the array of phases of each non-reference antenna An (1<n<=256) relative to the reference antenna A0. The first element of the array corresponds to the phase of antenna A1, the second element of the array corresponds to phase of antenna A2, and so on. relative amplitude (dB) — relative amplitude specifies the array of amplitudes of each non-reference antenna An (1<n<=256) relative to the reference antenna A0. The first element of the array corresponds to the amplitude of antenna A1, the second element of the array corresponds to amplitude of antenna A2, and so on. error in — error in describes error conditions that occur before this node runs. This input provides standard error in functionality. niBT SG session out — niBT SG session out returns the niBT SG session refnum. Use this reference as the session input to subsequent VIs. Note Close the niBT SG session refnum using the niBT SG Close Session VI before the VI completes execution to avoid possible memory leak issues. error out — error out contains error information. This output provides standard error out functionality. |
| --- |

Parent topic:

Configure Packet Settings

## TOPIC 00162: niBT SG Set Carrier Frequency Offset VI
